Southern Goods Industry Dismisses Large Number of Employees 126

Negotiations at a General Meeting Yesterday

More than 80 Southern Goods stores in this city, including Yu Da on Beijing Road, Tiancheng on Xinqiao Road, Zhisheng on Limei Road, Ruitai Xiang on Rue de la Sainte Famille, Maochang on Shanzhong Road, Wanyu Xiang in Zhabei, and Wannianfu in Tangjiawan, dismissed more than 240 employees during the abolished Lunar New Year holiday, citing sluggish business. The Southern Goods Industry Workers' Union dispatched personnel to negotiate with each store. Because some employers maintained a firm attitude, it was still difficult to resolve. In order to discuss effective countermeasures, the union held a representative meeting at its headquarters on Fuyou Road at 2:00 p.m. yesterday to discuss solutions. More than 200 representatives attended, and Yu Yaoqiu was elected to preside. The report stated that the employers of each store, clinging to custom, had dismissed a large number of workers without reason during the abolished Lunar New Year holiday, which was in violation of party and government instructions. It was proposed that they should jointly discuss countermeasures. After discussion, the following measures were resolved: (1) To immediately dispatch mediators to each store to conduct serious negotiations to achieve the purpose of resumption of work; (2) Before the dispute is resolved, the dismissed employees must remain in the store and must not leave without permission; (3) To send Gong Yimin, Shen Tao, and ten others to the industry association on the 23rd of this month to negotiate; (4) To investigate the implementation of conditions in each store; (5) To organize small groups in each district and take effective countermeasures when necessary; (6) To convene a temporary executive and supervisory meeting on the 24th; (7) To propose new conditions and methods to be discussed at the next general meeting. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Chiang Ting-wen Replied to the Fujian Fellow-Provincials Association, Endorsing Overseas Chinese Returning to China for Construction 127

The Minnan Shanghai Fellow-Provincials Association received a reply from Chiang Ting-wen yesterday, stating: "In reply, I have received your letter and fully understand your association's longing for your hometown and your intention to transfer funds back to China to prepare for autonomy, self-defense, and a model zone for the revival of rural construction and industry. The great plan and grand strategy, in addition to forwarding your intention to the provincial government for proper consideration, I will still do everything in my power to assist in all matters in order to comfort the feelings of the overseas Chinese. I am writing to inform you. Chiang Ting-wen Seal, addressed to the Minnan Shanghai Fellow-Provincials Association, the Overseas Chinese Federation, and the Overseas Minnan Overseas Chinese Association for National Salvation."

The Finance Bureau Plans to Draft Simplified Procedures for Collecting Land Value Tax 128

Since the commencement of land value tax collection in this city, the number of people paying the tax has been increasing daily. As the deadline is approaching, waiting to pay the tax has become very crowded. It is reported that the Finance Bureau previously considered the land value tax receipt to be of utmost importance to the taxpayer's property rights, so its procedures had to be carefully considered. Now, in view of the tense work of the various tax collection offices and in order to facilitate taxpayers, it is currently planning to draft other simplified procedures in order to be quick and comprehensive. It is also understood that the first phase of land value tax for the 23rd year [of the Republic] has been set to begin collection on March 1st.

Two Notices from the Jianghai Customs 129

Methods for Transshipping Goods

Special Regulations for Specific Customs Facilities

The General Affairs Section of the Jianghai Customs issued two proclamations one after the other on the previous two days. They are copied below: (1) Regarding the need to list the marks and numbers in detail for miscellaneous goods packages, it is verified that for miscellaneous goods packages that are reported for re-export to other commercial ports in the country, if they wish to enjoy the benefit of "paid import duties" (exemption from re-taxation), whether it is one or several bills of lading, the marks and numbers of each package must be clearly indicated upon import from overseas, so that they can be identified one by one. As for such packages that are not marked, they can also pay the fees according to regulations before submitting the declaration form, and the customs will send personnel to supervise and add the marks. If the marks and numbers are not listed in detail, the benefit of "paid import duties" will be lost. All merchants should pay attention to this. This is a special announcement. Deputy Tax Commissioner Zhou Li. (2) Regarding the issuance of special regulations for the management of special customs warehouses for the refining of crude oil into gasoline, etc., it is verified that the special regulations for the management of special customs warehouses for the refining of crude oil into gasoline, kerosene, diesel, etc. have now been ordered to be issued to the customs. Merchants can apply to the Deputy Tax Commissioner's Office of the General Affairs Section of this customs for these management regulations and their taxation methods. All should be informed. This is a special announcement. Deputy Tax Commissioner Zhou Li.

Ministry of Finance Approves Temporary Taxation of Fujian Tobacco Transported to Shanghai at the Request of the Chamber of Commerce 130

Because the Special Tax Has Not Yet Been Implemented in That Province

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the Leather Silk Tobacco Industry Association, stating that local tobacco from Fujian must still be taxed according to the non-special tax area method when transported to Shanghai, which tobacco merchants found difficult to bear. The Chamber immediately forwarded it to the Ministry of Finance for correction. It is now understood that the Chamber received a reply from the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating, "The submitted documents are all understood. When local tobacco leaves were changed to the special tax system, the seven provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Henan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Fujian were originally designated as special tax areas. Subsequently, due to the fact that Fujian Province did not comply with the regulations to uniformly change all local tobacco leaves in the province to the special tax system, and with the occurrence of the Fujian Incident and the resulting chaos, it was even more difficult to implement the special tax for a time. The Ministry stipulated that local tobacco leaves and their manufactured tobacco silk from the province, when transported into other special tax provinces, should be taxed uniformly according to the non-special tax area method by the first competent special tax agency at the point of entry. The order has been circulated for compliance. Now that the chaos in Fujian has been quelled, whether the special tax on local tobacco in the province can be prepared immediately has been ordered by the Ministry to the provincial Stamp Tax Bureau of Tobacco and Alcohol to closely examine the situation and submit a reply for approval. The previous circumstances as stated in the presentation should be forwarded to the association for notification. This approval."

Sixteen Banks Jointly Form a Syndicate to Borrow from the Italian Boxer Indemnity Fund 135

Seven Standing Committee Members Confer Once Yesterday

Issuing Securities, Not Public Bonds

Shenshi News Agency, local report: Sixteen banks in this city, including the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, are issuing 30 million yuan in securities with the 44 million yuan loan from the Ministry of Finance, guaranteed by the Italian Boxer Indemnity Fund. It is planned to start circulating on the market on the 1st of the month. Currently, for the needs of the facts, sixteen banks have resolved to organize a syndicate to handle all affairs. The syndicate is named the "Italian Boxer Indemnity Loan Syndicate." Each of the sixteen banks has sent one representative as an executive committee member, and the executive committee has elected seven people as standing committee members. Yesterday, the seven standing committee members held a conference at the Bank Club at No. 4 Hong Kong Road and elected Li Fuxun as chairman. The address of the syndicate is currently under negotiation and will be decided within a few days. According to a certain key figure within the syndicate who spoke to a reporter from the Shenshi News Agency yesterday, the securities issued by the sixteen banks this time are a type of company securities, not public bonds, because only the government has the right to issue public bonds, and the terminology and nature are clearly different and should not be confused.

Jiangsu Farmers Bank Prepares to Set Up an Agricultural Product Sales Office in Shanghai 138

No. 3 Peideli, Limei Road, Nanshi

In recent years, the rural economy has fallen into bankruptcy, which has attracted the attention of all parties. The reason for the bankruptcy of the rural economy is naturally due to the low prices of agricultural products and the inconvenience for farmers to directly transport and sell them to the market. Therefore, rescuing the rural economy by only focusing on circulating rural finance without paying attention to the transportation and sale of farmers' products will not thoroughly solve their livelihoods. In view of this, the Jiangsu Provincial Farmers Bank has specially prepared to set up the "Jiangsu Provincial Cooperative Agricultural Product Sales Office" so that farmers can receive help from the seedling stage to the production of grain sales. It is learned that the purpose of the Agricultural Product Sales Office is to specialize in acting as an agent for the transportation and sale of the products of the central transportation and sales cooperatives and farmers throughout the province. The preparatory office has already started work, located at No. 3 Peideli, Limei Road, Nanshi. The director is temporarily served concurrently by Hou Houpei, deputy manager of the Farmers Bank headquarters, and the deputy director is Mr. Hu Duming.

China Cooperative Wholesale Department Relocates 139

In order to facilitate the purchasing and wholesale matters for cooperative societies in various places, the China Cooperative Society established the "China Cooperative Wholesale Department" on the Xinhua Bank building on Jiangxi Road. The director of the department is Mr. Wang Zhixin. Since its opening, the business has been developing well. Those who entrust the department with purchasing and wholesale include the consumer cooperatives of employees of the Longhai and Jinpu Railways, the cooperative of the Central Political School, the Tongren consumer cooperative in Lanzhou, Gansu, the Zhejiang Second Tung Oil Production Cooperative, the Yongjia Ougan Sales Cooperative, and the Huangyan Orange Fruit Sales Cooperative, among other dozens of cooperatives. Currently, in order to cooperate with the Jiangsu Provincial Cooperative Agricultural Product Sales Office in business, the department has jointly rented a house with the office at No. 3 Peideli, Limei Road, Nanshi. It is reported that they have already moved in to work.

凌汛驟至長垣河工被冲壞 147

Sudden Ice Jam Damages Changyuan River Works

壩身尚穩固惟欵料亟待接濟

Dam Body Still Stable but Funds Urgently Needed

武陟縣洩水灌田工程已告竣

Wuzhi County Water Drainage and Irrigation Project Completed

Last year, the Yellow River flooded, inundating dozens of counties in Henan, Shandong, and Hebei provinces. The National Government specially formed the Yellow River Disaster Relief Committee to handle disaster relief and dike closure. In terms of work relief, except for the breaches at Changyuan and Shijiazhuang, the rest have been completed. The Shijiazhuang breach has been under construction, and during the ice jam period around the end of the lunar year, it was damaged by ice. The Disaster Relief Group in Wuzhi County, Henan Province, has completed the water drainage and irrigation project in the low-lying area, releasing over a hundred hectares of farmland. The details are as follows:

冰凌損害 148

Ice Damage

The work relief group reported the situation of the Fenglou project during the ice jam, according to Sun Qingze, Director of the Second District Works Department: "At 3 PM on the 12th, a piece of melting ice on the west bank of the third breach flowed to the west end of the ice prevention pile, breaking two sections of the railroad track and losing five large piles. The other end of the ice hit the dam body near Daoshu, but fortunately, it remained stable. After a while, the ice moved slightly again, breaking two middle large piles. Large pieces of ice have not yet flowed through the breach. If the ice melts and flows straight down, it is feared that all the piles will not be able to hold. However, the diversion channel is in good shape. The second and third diversion channels are 1.5 meters deeper than on the 9th. The water in the main river is rising daily. The water level at Shijiazhuang has not changed. At 3 PM on the 13th, large ice blocks below the diversion channel broke away from the edge and moved downwards. Nine more ice prevention piles were lost. Only two slanting, remaining piles are left west of the mouth of the cutoff dam, and six large piles remain on the east side of the mouth, and ten more to the east. The lost wooden piles and railroad tracks have all sunk into the water, and large pieces of ice are still stuck between the large piles of the cutoff dam. At 2 PM on the 14th, the ice in the main river moved, and seven more large piles at the Fenglou mouth were broken. The ice on the east and west wings piled up to the top, and several small piles of ice protection boards were broken. The dam body is stable, and the mouth has been washed by ice for three hours. Large pieces of ice are now stuck in between, slightly hindering the flow. The ice in the diversion channel and the main river has melted, and the situation is still good. However, funds are lacking and urgently need to be replenished."

洩水灌田 149

Water Drainage and Irrigation

Wuzhi County, Henan Province (west of the Pinghan Railway on the north bank of the Yellow River), has low-lying terrain. The floodwater after the Yellow River disaster has not receded completely. The area is twenty li from east to west and ten li from north to south, a vast expanse of water. The Yellow River Disaster Relief Group believed that the stagnant water not only made transportation inconvenient, but also made it difficult to plant wheat. In the spring, the evaporation of the water would cause a foul odor and be harmful to health. Therefore, they designed to dig rivers and canals to drain the stagnant water and irrigate the nearby fields. They recruited disaster victims to work, digging a main canal south of Bali Gang Village, about two li long. At the end point, they dug a horizontal canal, about eight zhang to the north and over a hundred zhang to the south. They dug several well openings in the horizontal canal and used water wheels to irrigate the nearby fields. It is said that it only took two weeks to complete the entire project, releasing over 11,000 mu of fertile land and irrigating over 2,000 mu of land next to the irrigation canal.

紅卍字會救濟隊在閩工作 150

Red Swastika Society Relief Team Working in Fujian

The Red Swastika Society previously sent two relief teams to Fujian Province due to the military disaster. It has been over a month. It is now reported that the Shanghai General Office of the Society received reports from the two teams yesterday, detailing the relief work in Fujian. The details are excerpted below: The North China Relief Team entered Fujian by land last month, passing through Quzhou to Jiangshan, then Pucheng, Jian'ou, and Yanping. It was found that Yanping was besieged by the Red Army from September to November. The food in the city was cut off, and the people were extremely distressed. The north and south passes were burned down, with over 500 civilian houses destroyed. The situation was tragic. The recent war made the people even more destitute. Team leader Nie Chengling sent personnel to investigate the disaster areas and found over 200 households with over 800 people in dire need of relief. Each person was given two yuan for emergency relief. The disaster situation in the seventh and eighth districts and Shunchang County was also serious and is currently under investigation. After arriving in Fuzhou, the Southeast Joint Relief Team organized two convalescent hospitals to treat wounded soldiers and civilians. However, wounded soldiers were scattered throughout the city, living in ancestral halls and nunneries, mostly without clothing or bedding. Six or seven out of ten died from injuries and illnesses. A temporary hospital has been established at the Fuzhou Xiadu Fire Brigade to accommodate soldiers and civilians with serious illnesses. After they recover, they will be sent back to their hometowns. It has been found that soldiers from the 19th Route Army with household registration in Guangdong have all been sent back to Guangdong. Most of the rest remain in the provincial capital. In addition, many civilian houses in Xiadou Town, thirty li from the province, were burned down, and the people had no place to live. An investigation found 33 extremely poor households with a total of 78 people. They were divided into "Swastika" and "Relief" categories. "Swastika" category: 5 yuan per large mouth, 2 yuan per small mouth. "Relief" category: 4 yuan per large mouth, 2 yuan per small mouth. Furthermore, no less than several thousand refugees from the bandit disasters in Tai Ning, Jian Ning, and Chong'an counties fled to the province one after another. They have been stranded for over a year and cannot return. Local public groups have established 26 reception centers, but there are still several hundred people outside who have not been accommodated. Many of them are sick. The team has sent personnel to distribute 1,800 bottles of emergency medicine to each center and has selectively provided relief money to the elderly, weak, women, and children for medical treatment. In addition, the military excavation of trenches around the Longshan waist in Fuzhou destroyed hundreds of graves. The team has sent personnel to bury them. Xiangsi Ridge in Yongtai Town was an area of fierce fighting between the two armies, with over a thousand casualties. Although the local authorities have buried them, there are still corpses in the mountain streams and thickets. The team has sent laborers to bury them.

濟生會續辦贛省工振 151

Jisheng Society Continues Work Relief in Jiangxi Province

The China Jisheng Society has been carrying out work relief in Jiangxi Province for the past year to repair embankments. The three embankments, Dayou, Fuyou, and Guangfeng, have been completed one after another. It has been over a year and a considerable amount of money has been spent. The Guangfeng Embankment sluice gate could not be completed at the time because the water had already surged up, making it impossible to work. Now, the Society, in order to prevent the surge of spring water, must rush to complete the project. Therefore, it has been decided that Mr. Li Yunmen will be publicly recommended to take charge on the 23rd of this month to continue the work and complete it as soon as possible. However, China's water conservancy, such as the counties of Heze in western Shandong and the various prefectures of Henan Province, has not been repaired in many places. The spring water is expected to be dangerous soon, and disaster victims are everywhere. Farmers have no hope of production. It is hoped that patriotic people and those who are enthusiastic about charity will rise up and work hard to continue their work.

公共租界衛生狀况 153

Public Concession Health Conditions

上月份天花蔓延頗烈

Smallpox Epidemic Quite Severe Last Month

The Public Works Department's Health Department's work report for January stated: "The public has been warned about the spread of smallpox. In late January, it spread quite severely. Although the public has paid attention to this, only 16,730 people have been vaccinated by the Health Department, which cannot be considered many. The municipal water supply had a salty taste at the end of January. This is a common phenomenon every year due to the shallow water of the Yangtze River and the high tide. A physical examination of students was held at the Huade Road Primary School, with a total of 662 students. The results are currently being considered. What can be said is that the proportion of students suffering from preventable diseases is too high.

生死統計 154

Birth and Death Statistics

The number of births is estimated at 19.07 per thousand for foreigners. This number is still below the actual number because births may not be attended by doctors. For the Chinese, 177 births were reported. This is only a small fraction of the total number. The reason for this record is to hope that the public and the medical community will be aware of this registration system and cooperate to gradually obtain more reliable numbers. The death rate for foreigners is 12.38, which is lower than the average. For the Chinese, as far as is known, it is 16.33, which is higher than the same month last year, but still lower than the average. The most common deaths from infectious diseases are tuberculosis, smallpox, and typhoid fever.

傳染病症 155

Infectious Diseases

Smallpox and influenza have increased among foreigners. Among the Chinese, there were 63 reported cases of smallpox, with 42 deaths. Among them, 30 were sent to the Chinese Isolation Hospital. It was found that only 6 had been vaccinated against smallpox, and all were vaccinated in their youth. Scarlet fever has increased seasonally, but not drastically. As for influenza, as many as 10 Chinese people died from it. In addition, rashes have also increased sharply. Parents of all schoolchildren must pay attention to the initial fever of children and take precautions early to avoid many dangers.

病理研究 156

Pathological Research

The Pathological Research Laboratory tested a total of 3,765 samples and 1,914 rats. 60 samples of breast milk and 27 samples of tap water were tested. The Chemical Testing Laboratory conducted 309 tests. The Rabies Clinic received a total of 20 patients, 18 of whom were advised to seek treatment. 8 people completed treatment and 8 people received preventive treatment, but 2 people left without completing treatment.

食品檢查 157

Food Inspection

The production of milk this month exceeded all previous records. The samples were subjected to bacterial examination and were very satisfactory, even for grade B milk. However, after chemical examination, 4 grade B milk samples failed. The supply of meat was normal, but the number of pigs slaughtered increased by 8% due to the approaching Spring Festival. The situation in the vegetable markets was quite satisfactory. Bakeries were still inspected in the early morning and at night. Cases of violating licensing regulations were tried quickly in the Special District Court, which greatly benefited the work of the Licensing Department.

飯館衛生 158

Restaurant Hygiene

The Health Department is seeking to improve the conditions of Chinese restaurants of all kinds and to require them to have special rooms for raw vegetables. Several groups have expressed objections. In fact, the Health Department's reporting and implementation of these improvement procedures are giving detailed consideration to the situation of each restaurant. Except for those in very poor condition, all are being gradually changed to avoid difficulties. After all, it would be very difficult to suddenly order large-scale reforms in old stores that have been around for many years.

Northeast Anti-Japanese Heroes Wang Zhenqiu and Others Arrive in Shanghai from Beiping

寓居旅邸中情形悽慘

Miserable Situation Residing in Hotels

向許世英朱子橋呼籲

Appealing to Xu Shiying and Zhu Ziqiao

Wounded soldiers from the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army led by Ma Zhanshan, Zhu Jiqing, Feng Yong, and others have been successively sent back to their hometowns and found other means of livelihood after being treated in various hospitals in Beiping. Currently, Wang Zhenqiu, Dai Enrong, Yuan Zhenhai, Li Qishan, and 34 others have come to Shanghai to make a living after being treated in hospitals in Beiping. According to them, "Our hometowns are mostly in the Northeast, which has now fallen into the territory of the puppet state. Because we cannot return to our hometowns and we are all disabled, it is difficult to make a living. We have no choice but to come to Shanghai to make a living. We are residing in hotels, living alone and relying on each other. Life is difficult. We are now appealing to Shanghai philanthropists Xu Shiying, Zhu Ziqiao, and others to find a way to provide relief so that we can maintain our lives." It is learned that Xu and others, recognizing that the end of a hero is the same throughout history, have agreed to find a way to arrange for them.

謀剌前財宋要犯劉剛由厦解滬 165

Liu Gang, the Main Criminal in the Plot to Assassinate Former Finance Minister Song, Escorted to Shanghai from Xiamen

二月三日經厦市公安局緝獲

Arrested by the Xiamen Public Security Bureau on February 3rd

前日解滬現押市公安局候訊

Escorted to Shanghai the Day Before Yesterday and Now Detained in the Municipal Public Security Bureau Awaiting Interrogation

Since the major case of plotting to assassinate former Finance Minister Song Ziwen at the North Railway Station, in which Song's confidential secretary Tang Yulu was shot and killed on the spot, the police agencies of this city have conducted investigations and successively arrested many people. However, the main criminal in this case, named Liu Gang, remained at large. A secret order was issued to strictly arrest and bring him to justice. It was unexpected that Liu had fled to other ports after the incident and finally hid in Xiamen. It was not until February 3rd of this year that Huang Bin and Hu Zhen, officers of the Xiamen Public Security Bureau, learned of his whereabouts and arrested him. On the 12th, they urgently telegraphed Mayor Wu Tiecheng and Public Security Bureau Chief Wen Hongen. 錢紹豐大仇已雪判處徒刑七年 166

Qian Shaofeng's Great Revenge Has Been Avenged, Sentenced to Seven Years in Prison

激於義憤甘冒萬險

Driven by Righteous Indignation, Willing to Risk Everything

錢樹聲律師之陳情

Attorney Qian Shusheng's Petition

Qian Shaofeng, also known as Peihao, a 21-year-old college student from An'nan County, Guizhou, whose father, Qian Bin, served as the Director of the Finance Bureau of An'nan, was killed on March 5th, 1931 by the county magistrate, He Zunfu, a fellow villager, under the pretext of carrying out orders from superiors, in collusion with Zhou Haitao, the company commander of the local garrison. Shaofeng, determined to avenge his father, went out to study alone, traveling to Beiping, Hubei, Nanjing, and other places. He came to Shanghai last year and resided at No. 13 Yuanchang Lane, Hualong Road, French Concession. On the evening of October 16th, he encountered his enemy, He Zunfu, watching a movie at the Golden Grand Theater in Baxianqiao. Shaofeng followed him with a knife, bought a ticket to enter the theater, and hid behind He. Taking the opportunity, he stabbed He to death to avenge his father. After committing the crime, he abandoned the murder weapon and was intercepted by patrols when he fled the theater. He was taken to the police station and sent to the Second Special District Local Court, where he was prosecuted for murder. After questioning, the court sent a document to the An'nan government to investigate whether Qian's father was indeed killed by He and Zhou, and received a reply to the case. The trial resumed on the 12th of this month. Because the plaintiff, He Rong (He Zunfu's son), did not have his lawyer present, the defendant hired lawyer Qian Shusheng to defend him, stating that the defendant was driven by righteous indignation and willing to risk everything. His actions were sufficient to request a reduction in punishment. The debate was adjourned until the next day, and the closing arguments were heard pending sentencing. The situation has been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday was the sentencing date. At 10 AM, the police sent a detective to escort Qian to the court. Presiding Judge Wang Gangxu presided over the First Criminal Court and sentenced Qian Shaofeng to seven years in prison for murder. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be deducted from the sentence at a rate of two days for one day. The murder weapon will be confiscated. After the sentencing, the defendant was ordered to be transferred to the detention center pending further instructions during the appeal period.

British Police Court Continues Trial of Major Fraud Case

大美晚報云、英領署警務法庭今晨復審訊普西洋行英人馬克被控向麥加利銀行騙取巨欵案、先由證人柯明西安氏聲稱、有會計員名歐白者、以假支票數紙付之、繼乃逃逸、後由法捕房查明其人居吕班路第七號公寓第二百五十六房間、而致函英美烟公司謀求職業、藉以賺得該公司要員簽名覆函之凱萊女士、卽住是室云、次由美人沃特森氏聲稱、渠與其弟皆爲普西洋行董事、馬克案發後、均已辭職、行中事務、由馬克一手掌管、渠昆仲曾收到馬克所付董事公費支票一紙、計八百元、該票乃由索柯洛夫簽名云、次由彫刻師日人某氏證明渠承接二俄人委製雕刻版之情形、馬克所僱用之意人唐布里尼氏父子、將由意領署法庭、於下星期二日審訊、又麥加利銀行僱員葡人巴浦蒂斯太氏、現由葡領署法庭審訊、下星期將解往澳門續審、

The Two-Route Administration Improves the Songhu Branch Line 168

Thirteen Improvement Cases Resolved

The Traffic Department of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Two-Route Administration, in order to improve the Songhu branch line of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, specially convened a traffic meeting to discuss the following improvement cases: (1) The line is very short, with few first-class passengers, and seats are often wasted. It is proposed to reduce the original sixteen first-class seats by eight, and at the same time expand third-class seats to make adjustments. (The Administration ordered the complete abolition of first-class seats, regardless of class, charging all fares at the third-class rate, and at the same time increasing equipment on the vehicles, striving for cleanliness, which shall be handled jointly by the Mechanical and Traffic Departments.) (2) The turnout lines at each station on the branch line, except for the Jiangwan Station, are very short, only enough for two steam locomotives to stop. When trains meet that are longer than two steam locomotives, accidents are likely to occur. If both trains are longer than two steam locomotives, they cannot meet. It is proposed to lengthen them to facilitate traffic. Also, the platforms at Gaoxing Temple and Yunzaobang stations are too short, making it inconvenient for passengers to get on and off, and they must also be lengthened to ensure safety. (The Administration ordered the Engineering Department to study and estimate the costs for review.) (3) The railings at each station on the line are mostly very short, causing passengers to leave the station without going through the ticket barrier. It is not easy to crack down on those riding without tickets. It is proposed to extend the railings at each station to the branching points at both ends, and set up gates, operated by the switchmen, and prohibit idlers from entering and exiting to prevent abuses. (The Administration ordered the Engineering Department to study and estimate the costs.) (4) Although the applicable period of validity for regular tickets on the line is clearly stated on the ticket, the font is small and not easily noticed in a hurry, making it easy for holders to misuse them. It is proposed to add prominent large characters to these tickets to make them easier to identify, and to use two-sided transparent clear corner sleeves to prevent damage and blurring. (The Accounting Department was ordered to follow this procedure when printing tickets.) (5) Passengers on the line often carry local products and goods, and vendors often bring goods onto the train. Because of the regulations, they must pay freight, which often leads to disputes. It is now proposed to formulate other measures so that baggage that can be carried by one person and does not take up space will be exempt from freight to benefit merchants and travelers. (The Traffic Department was ordered to revise and submit detailed remedial measures for review.) In addition, attention should be paid to locomotives and coal to avoid delays, and the original steam locomotives should be repaired to increase the number of trips. The Mechanical Department was ordered to handle this diligently. As for personnel matters, the Traffic Department plans to redistribute them, and it has been approved to handle this carefully within the shortest possible time.

New Development of the Fruit and Produce Industry, Exporting Domestically Produced Fruit to England for Trial Sales 169

Notice to Gentlemen and Ladies of All Nations to Try Chinese Specialties

Replicating Foreign Market Decorations for Beauty and Hygiene

The International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, given that our country's fruits are rarely sold overseas, resulting in the absence of Chinese fruits in overseas markets, in order to seek overseas development, convened leaders of fruit merchants in this city in mid-October of last year to discuss ways to open overseas fruit markets. It was decided to first try selling to Liverpool, England. Preparations have been completed to date. The following is an inquiry to the industry for details:

Decorating for Export to England: According to the person in charge of the Fruit and Produce Industry Association of this city, the fruit for trial sales to England, which was decided last year, includes Ya pears, chestnuts, ginkgo nuts, and dried jujubes. They were prepared long ago, but have been delayed due to the lack of refrigerated compartments on the ships. On the 11th of this month, a British Taikoo liner sailed from Shanghai to England, with many refrigerated compartments, which can store fruit for a long time without spoiling. It was decided to ship the above types of fruit on this liner.

Notice to All Nations: After the industry shipped the above-mentioned fruits by British liner, in order to promote the attention of people of all countries to the advantages of Chinese fruits, a notice was issued, stating, "China is located in the temperate zone, with fertile soil and abundant agricultural products and fresh vegetables. The pears and chestnuts of Tianjin, the long pears of Shandong, the pomelos of Guangdong, the Guangqiao of Shantou, the peaches and apricots of Zhejiang, and other famous fruits from various places are all well-known at home and abroad. Their excellent quality and delicious flavor have long been admired by foreign countries. Modern planting methods are improving day by day, and attention to preservation and hygiene is also extremely complete. We have specially selected famous fruits from the four seasons to present to the gentlemen and ladies of Europe and America. We hope you will try them."

Beautiful Decoration: The pears for this trial sale to England are divided into three types: No. 1, No. 2, and No. 3, all packed in wooden boxes. No. 1 has 200 pears per box, No. 2 has 250 pears per box, and No. 3 has 300 pears per box. Chestnuts and ginkgo nuts are packed in burlap sacks, each weighing 100 pounds. The decorations used are no different from those commonly used in the British market, and are extremely beautiful and lovely. The trademark adopts the Boy Scout brand, with a drawing of a Boy Scout holding a wooden stick, showing British spirit and boldness. Each fruit package has a label attached for easy identification.

Fruit Characteristics: The origin of the above fruits is as follows: Pears are produced in Shandong, green when raw, turning yellow when ripe, with a pointed shape and a round stem. When eating, the skin and core are removed. Boiling the juice is called pear paste, which can be used for medicinal purposes. Eating raw quenches thirst and generates fluids, and eating cooked clears the lungs and resolves phlegm, tastes delicious and is full of juice. Chestnuts are produced in Zhejiang, Tianjin, and other places. Eating cooked benefits qi and tonifies the kidneys, and is the most beneficial of all fruits. Ginkgo nuts are produced in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, with a pointed and round shape. The flesh is light green when tender, turning yellow over time. They can only be eaten cooked, warming the lungs and benefiting qi, and providing beneficial nutrition.

Doctor of Incantations Jiang Lichu Shot and Killed by Robbers 170

The Robbers Ultimately Stole Nothing, Took Not a Penny

The Maid Li Hu's Right Cheek Also Struck by a Bullet

Jiang Lichu, a native of Yangzhou, was 53 years old and lived at No. 5, Lane 330 (Pingle Lane), Xizang Road, in the Public Concession. He practiced incantation medicine, and his livelihood was fairly good. Suddenly, yesterday at about 3:30 PM, five robbers came, each holding a pistol, wearing blue and black cloth gowns, and wearing woolen hats, speaking with a local accent. One robber was on guard at the front door, one was guarding the back door, and three robbers went straight to Jiang's consulting room in the west wing downstairs. At that time, Jiang was taking a nap and had not gotten up. Only Jiang's youngest daughter was in the consulting room. The robbers immediately asked the girl if she was surnamed Jiang, and forbade her to make a sound. The girl, seeing this situation, knew things were not good, and could not help but cry out. Jiang heard his beloved daughter's cry in the back room, hurriedly put on his clothes and walked out. The robbers had already entered the back room. Jiang immediately grabbed the wrist of one robber. While they were struggling, the robber next to him fired a shot at the floor, ordering Jiang to let go. The robbers retreated to the front consulting room, and Jiang also followed. Suddenly, the robber guarding the back door, hearing the gunshot inside, thought that the matter had gone wrong, and planned to go through the reception hall to investigate. At that time, Li Hu, a 60-year-old maid surnamed Qi, was walking down from upstairs. The robber, seeing her, immediately grabbed her, asking her if she was surnamed Jiang and where she lived, and ordered her to lead the way. At this time, Jiang and the robbers had already struggled from the consulting room to the reception hall, and at the same time, two robbers had already walked out the front door, and two robbers were also about to leave the house. Jiang and the old woman Li Hu, in shock and confusion, lost their minds and unconsciously followed them out. When the robbers saw this, thinking that they were about to be followed and arrested, they were greatly panicked, and fired a shot at the maid Li Hu first. The bullet entered from her right cheek and exited from the root of her left ear, and she fell to the ground on the spot, bleeding profusely. Jiang Lichu, seeing this, immediately retreated and crouched under the window. Suddenly, the second shot flew from his side, hitting Jiang's right chest. The bullet did not exit, and he fell to the ground in a pool of blood on the spot. The robbers then calmly escaped. When the police arrived after receiving the news, the robbers had long since fled. They immediately reported to the police station, and a car was sent to rush Jiang and the old woman Li Hu to Renji Hospital on Shandong Road for treatment. However, Jiang died on the way due to his serious injuries, and was sent to the coroner's office to await examination. The old woman Li Hu was not in serious condition. After hearing the news, the reporter went to investigate. According to Jiang's youngest daughter, the robbers never stole a penny or anything, and it was impossible to guess what they meant. She pointed out the location where her father was injured, where blood was flowing all over the ground, and the stench was overwhelming. A woolen hat worn by the maid Li Hu was still soaked in blood, and the scene was extremely tragic.

Wu Huatai Suggests Setting Up a Fire Safety Net 171

If a Ten-Story Building is Careless

A Net Opens to Ensure Absolute Safety

Lawyer Wu Huatai wrote in a letter to the editor of Shen Bao, saying, "Dear Editor of Shen Bao, I, Huatai, having seen the shortcomings in Shanghai's fire-fighting equipment, am now writing to the fire departments of the Chinese and foreign concessions to make a suggestion. The letter reads: I am writing to inform you that the Shanghai area is well-maintained in terms of safety, and the fire department can be said to be unique. They arrive as soon as they are reported, and can extinguish the fire in a few minutes. The quality of their work is such that even in the West, it is no more than this. However, in recent years, new buildings in Shanghai have tended to increase in height. Residential buildings have four or five stories, and skyscrapers with more than ten stories are even more impressive. Such prosperity and large-scale construction cannot be said to be a bad phenomenon for the city, but it inevitably has some shortcomings in terms of fire protection. In the event of a fire on the lower floors, it is often difficult for those on the top floors to escape. Although the fire department has rescue ladders, when there are many people and they are anxious and panicked, they all want to be the first to escape, and will certainly not be able to maintain order and climb the ladder one by one. In such a situation, it is inevitable that not everyone can be guaranteed safety. Furthermore, for high buildings with more than ten stories, I am afraid that the fire department's ladders will not reach. At this time, a rescue net is indispensable. The rescue net (also known as a safety net) is made of extremely thick ropes, tied into a grid of five or six zhang in length and width. When the building is too high for the ladder to reach, this net can be used, with hooks on the four corners, or pulled open by manpower, so that those who cannot escape can jump down from above and be safe. This equipment is small in area and costs very little, and is truly easy and inexpensive, and greatly benefits fire protection. Rather than digging a well when thirsty, it is better to prepare for a rainy day. Moreover, this method has been practiced in Western countries for a long time, but the fire departments in Shanghai have not yet done so. In my opinion, Shanghai is a major trading port with a dense population and prosperous commerce, and should plan for this as soon as possible. If it has not been created in the past, it should be emulated in the future. Therefore, I dare to offer my humble opinion, and I do not know whether I can invite your department to adopt and prepare it. I am writing this letter with great anticipation. Sincerely, (Omitted below) I think your newspaper is the voice of the citizens, and will certainly support this. I hope you will promote it with sympathy to promote its success. Whether it is appropriate or not, please advise. I am very grateful. Respectfully wishing you good writing."

The Largest and Heaviest Ship Repaired at the Shanghai Dockyard 172

528 Feet Long and 63 Feet Wide

Gross Weight Estimated at 11,500 Tons

The Zi Lin Daily News reported that the Blue Funnel Line's Philoctetes, which was recently damaged in a collision with the China Merchants Bureau's Puan steamer outside the Songkou, is currently being repaired at the Yesson Dockyard. The ship belongs to Alfred Holt & Co. of Liverpool, England, and is one of the largest and heaviest ships to enter the Shanghai Dockyard for repairs. The ship is 528 feet long, 63 feet wide, and has a gross weight of 11,500 tons. It will take about a week to leave the dock, and then other repairs will be carried out, so it will not be able to leave Shanghai for a while.

Qi Chufa and Others' Case of Privately Destroying National Currency 174

Postponed Due to Unreceived Reply from the Ministry of Finance

Each Defendant Ordered to Remain on Original Bail

Qi Chufa of Shaoxing, due to setting up the Ruitai Silver Furnace at No. 20, Yixing Lane, Qipulu, and No. 41, Tiantong Road, specializing in melting silver ingots, was previously discovered by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Because Qi and others violated the order issued by the Ministry of Finance to abolish taels and change to yuan, they dispatched Detective Hu Kui Sheng at 7:30 PM on the 2nd of this month, reported to the First Special District Court, signed out a search warrant, and, with the assistance of Chinese Detective Liang Yuliang of the Municipal Police Station, went to the above two places and arrested the owners Qi Chufa, Qian Guoxun, Zhou Huilin, Chen Jinshan, Shen Yushu, Tong Dasheng, and others, confiscating 26 silver ingots, 879 double-cornered silvers, 62 pounds of broken silver, and clay models, and brought them to the Special Court. After a preliminary interrogation, Qi was ordered to pay 3,000 yuan bail, Qian, Chen, and Shen each paid 500 yuan bail, and Zhou and Tong each paid a shop guarantee to be summoned at any time and waited for interrogation. All the details have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday morning was the date of the continued interrogation. The Public Works Department was still represented by Lawyer Jiang Baolian, and the defendants were represented by Lawyers Yan Yiping and Wu Baotai. The Municipal Public Security Bureau also appointed Legal Counsel Zhan Jifeng to appear in court and requested a postponement. Trial Judge Wu Tingqi immediately announced, "This case is being postponed. This court has sent a letter to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to submit evidence. According to the reply, it stated that this case has been reported to the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance, asking about the ban on privately destroying national currency and the measures to be taken. The reply has not yet been received, so this case must still be postponed." He then ordered each defendant to remain on their original bail and wait for the rescheduled hearing on the morning of March 13.

Taikoo Yuezhou New Ship Arrives in Shanghai 175

Sailing Between Shanghai and Annam

Maiden Voyage on the 23rd

The British Taikoo Steamship Company, whose shipping operations on various rivers and seas last year were deeply affected by the economic downturn and the Guangzhou strike, found it difficult to make a profit overall, suffering considerable losses. However, they have been constantly researching and improving the ships used, gradually decommissioning older ships that consumed more coal and building new-style ships that were more fuel-efficient and had greater productivity. Two new ocean liners have been added to the North and South Seas routes, one being the Yuezhou, built by the Glasgow Dockyard in the United Kingdom, with a displacement of 2,800 tons, a length of 298 feet, a width of 44 feet, and a draft of 17 feet, with 17 officer cabins. The ship is mainly used for cargo transportation and has great speed, capable of traveling 14 nautical miles per hour, while being extremely fuel-efficient. In order to develop the South China shipping industry, the ship has been specially assigned to sail from Shanghai to Swatow and Guangzhou, and then to Haikou and Beihai, and directly to Haiphong to connect the Shanghai-Annam route. There are many overseas Chinese traveling on this route, and there are no ships sailing from Shanghai. The ship arrived in Shanghai from London yesterday and began loading cargo today. It is scheduled to depart from Shanghai on its maiden voyage to Haiphong at 10:00 AM on the 23rd. The cargo has already been fully loaded. Furthermore, the company's North Seas regular ship, after adding the new Shengyang ship last year, has greater productivity. Therefore, a new ocean liner of the same type has been ordered from its own factory in Hong Kong, named the Xin Shuntian, which can arrive in Shanghai in May of this year and be assigned to the Shanghai-Yantai-Qingdao-Tianjin route to compete in the market.

The Consolidated Tax Bureau Returns Detained Cigarettes 176

The Shanghai South Office of the Municipal Cigarette Trade Association previously received a letter from its member, Xielongchang, a freight forwarder at Cuifeng Wharf, requesting the return of 2,000 Small Beauty cigarettes that had been seized. The office immediately forwarded the situation to the Su-Zhe-Wan Consolidated Tax Bureau for certification and requested the return. They have now received a reply stating, "Merchants who wholesale and retail cigarettes should issue customers invoices with official stamps, so that they can be verified along the way. In this case, Xielongchang sold 2,000 Small Beauty cigarettes, but did not transport them with boxes bearing the verification stamp, nor did they issue an invoice with an official stamp, making it impossible to verify them. It was inappropriate to detain them. Since your association has sent boxes for verification and provided a letter of certification, after the boxes have been inspected by the Shanghai Inspection Office, they will be returned. Xielongchang should also be informed that when reselling cigarettes in the future, they must follow the prescribed procedures and not make any more mistakes." In addition to instructing the Shanghai Inspection Office, a corresponding letter has been replied. The association, based on this, immediately forwarded a letter to the company asking them to send someone to the office to retrieve the detained cigarettes, and instructed them to comply with the prescribed procedures in the future and not make any more mistakes, so as not to cause disputes.

The Two-Route Administration Bridge Demolition Dispute Escalates 177

More Than a Thousand Residents of Dayang Bridge Prevented Work Yesterday

Visiting Wang Binyan to Beg for Help and Submitting a Petition to the Administration

The residents of the Jiaotong Road area, due to the Two-Route Administration's construction of a concrete wall of more than 200 zhang along Jiaotong Road, are protesting the demolition of the wooden bridge on the east side of Dayang Bridge. The bridge crosses the railway and allows residents of Panjiawan in the south to interact with each other, with about 10,000 people passing through daily. It benefits merchants, facilitates workers, and maintains commerce. If the bridge is demolished, the livelihoods of more than a hundred merchants in the vicinity will be cut off. Therefore, they have repeatedly asked the Administration to avoid demolition, but to no avail. Yesterday, workers were building the wall in the area and demolishing the bridge, which was seen by all the residents, who urgently gathered more than a thousand people to prevent it. A serious dispute was about to occur. Fortunately, the Public Security Bureau suppressed it and it was temporarily averted. The details are as follows:

Preventing Bridge Demolition 178

At 10:00 AM yesterday, about 30 workers from the Administration came again to the area to demolish the bridge, which aroused the reaction of the residents of Panjiawan, who gathered about a thousand people to prevent it. A serious dispute was about to occur. Fortunately, the Third Division of the Fourth District was informed and dispatched Patrol Officer Xu Yuanlin and more than a dozen policemen to maintain order, preventing an accident. The residents dispersed at 12:00 PM, and the workers stopped work and reported to their superiors.

Merchants Meeting 179

More than a hundred shops in the Dayang Bridge area, including Hesheng Zhenchang, etc., convened an emergency meeting because repeated negotiations with the Administration to avoid demolishing the bridge were ineffective. They decided to petition the Administration to stop the demolition and to seek assistance from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and various municipal authorities.

Residents' Petition 180

Yesterday, about 300 residents of Panjiawan went to the Zhabei Ciku Troupe on Datong Road and petitioned Wang Binyan, asking for assistance. Wang received them and promised to negotiate with the Administration regarding their intentions. The residents were satisfied and left.

Letter to the Administration 181

Yesterday, the residents of Panjiawan also sent a letter to the Administration stating, "We, several thousand households, have lived for generations in the Panjiawan area at the end of Maigen Road in Zhabei. The only way in and out is a small wooden bridge to the north. The east, south, and west are all surrounded by the Suzhou River. Now that your administration is building a wall to protect the road, the livelihoods of several thousand households will inevitably be cut off. We earnestly request that you leave a small opening in the wall, so that the people can cross the bridge and reach the prosperous road. This would also be the virtue of the director. (Omitted) This is addressed to the Director of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Two-Route Administration. Representatives of the residents of Panjiawan in Zhabei, Shanghai: Chen Genbao, Zhang Xianglin, Pan Shangqing, Jiang Zuomei, and more than sixty others."

Social Affairs Bureau Recruits Consumer Cooperative Instructors 182

Six Positions Allotted, Seven Examination Questions

The Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau plans to recruit six instructors to be sent to designated factories to guide workers in organizing consumer cooperatives, as workers in various factories are unclear about organizational laws and regulations. The recruitment method is as follows: (1) Qualifications: University or high school graduates, or equivalent education, with considerable research and experience in cooperation. (2) Salary: Temporarily set at 40 yuan per month. (3) Application Procedures: First, select four questions from the following test questions, along with a four-inch full-body photo and detailed resume and address, and send them to the Bureau by March 5. After review and qualification, a special letter will be sent to notify the date of the retest. Those who do not qualify will not be notified. The test questions are as follows: (1) A factory has 1,200 workers, one-quarter of whom are female. It is now planned to establish a worker consumer cooperative. How should it be established? Please submit a detailed plan and implementation steps. (2) How should the factory assist workers in establishing a consumer cooperative? Please explain the reasons and methods. (Applicants should answer both of the above questions in full.) (3) Cooperative enterprises and national salvation. (4) Is the Rochdale Principles suitable for operating consumer cooperatives in our country? Please explain in detail. (5) In the urban environment, it is quite difficult to operate consumer cooperatives. How should it be done? Please explain. (6) Prepare a publicity plan for worker cooperation in this city. (7) A brief introduction to worker consumer cooperatives. (Applicants can select two questions from the above five questions, completing a total of four questions.)

The Chinese Photography Yearbook Edited by Hu Boxiang Has Been Printed 186

Photography is the most popular art internationally. Countries in Europe, America, and Japan all publish photography yearbooks annually to promote their photographic arts internationally. One can glimpse their artistic culture through these yearbooks. The earliest British photography yearbook has been published for seventy-three years, and the Japanese photography yearbook has reached its eighth year. When Europeans and Americans discuss Eastern photographic art, they often take Japanese works as representative, which is the merit of the yearbook. The Chinese photography community has long discussed publishing a yearbook, but due to various printing and distribution difficulties, it has not been realized. Last year, the Chinese Art Society prepared for publication, and with the support of contemporary master of Chinese painting and pioneer of artistic photography, Mr. Hu Boxiang, who agreed to be the chief editor, along with Zhu Shuren, a well-known researcher of photography, as the assistant editor, progress was very rapid. The yearbook's selection of materials is purely based on openness, with extremely broad collection and strict selection. Many works that are admired by peers but rarely seen by the public are included. The masterpieces of various artists include Qian Kanghou, Lin Hanlun, Huang Bohui, Gan Naiguang, Ding Song, Cai Junshan, Guo Shuliang, Guo Xiqi, Jiang Baoli, Zeng Zhongming, Shen Gao, Zhang Zhenhou, Huang Zhongzhang, Wu Zhongxing, Hu Boxizhou, Qian Jinghua, Lang Jingshan, Shu Xincheng, Fu Bingchang, Lu Shifu, Chen Wanli, Tong Boqu, Chen Chuanlin, Hu Junlei, Cai Jielu, Zhu Liwo, Zhang Liyun, Shao Woyun, and several well-known foreign writers such as Deng Tuo and Jia Hualu, totaling about seventy artists. The yearbook is printed entirely with two-color special editions and the finest paper. Printing has now begun, and it is said that after the yearbook's sample pages were sent to Europe and America, numerous congratulatory letters of praise from various countries have been received. The society is even more encouraged and expects to publish the book around March.

Ministry of Communications Stipulates Measures for Ship Markings 187

The Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau of the Ministry of Communications issued a bulletin yesterday stating, "The Ministry of Communications issued Instruction No. 634, stating that ship markings are an important part of ship equipment, as stipulated in Article 6 of the Ship Law, and Article 37 of the same law clearly states the penalties. The Ministry has now formulated six articles for the Ship Marking Measures, which have already been announced by the Ministry. This bureau is instructed to notify all shipping companies to comply with the measures," and attached five copies of the Ship Marking Order to the bureau. In addition to distributing the order, the Ship Marking Measures are extracted for public knowledge, and all shipping companies are instructed to comply. The bulletin is hereby issued, and the six articles of the Ship Marking Measures are copied below: Article 1: The ship markings stipulated in Article 6 of the Ship Law shall be handled in accordance with these measures. Article 2: The location of ship markings is as follows: 1. The ship's name shall be marked on the central part of both the left and right sides, and on the central part of the stern. If Western text is used, the Western text should be marked on both sides of the bow and below the center of the stern. 2. The name of the port of registry shall be marked below the ship's name on the stern. Western text may be used below the Chinese text. 3. The ship's registered tonnage and number shall be marked in Arabic numerals in a conspicuous place on the wheelhouse. 4. The draft scale shall be marked in Roman numerals at both ends of the bow and stern. The height of the numerals shall be limited to six feet, and the lower end of the numerals shall indicate the number of feet. The Western text in the first item and the second item of the preceding paragraph shall not be larger than the area occupied by the Chinese text. Article 3: The location of sailboat markings is as follows: 1. The ship's name and port of registry shall be marked on both sides near the stern or in the center of the stern. 2. The ship's registered burden and number shall be marked on both sides of the bow or on both sides of the cabin. Sailboat markings shall all use Chinese characters. Article 4: Ship markings shall be provided by the shipowner in accordance with these measures. The color of the markings shall be limited to black, white, or brass. Article 5: After the implementation of these measures, ship registration plates for steamships and sailboats shall be immediately invalidated. Article 6: These measures shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Yan Fuqing's Anti-Tuberculosis Speech 192

The Anti-Tuberculosis Association invited Dr. Yan Fuqing, President of the Chinese Red Cross Hospital, to give a lecture at the Gospel Broadcasting Station on the evening of the 17th at 8 PM. The lecture was very detailed. Here is a brief summary of his speech: According to the world's tuberculosis mortality statistics, China ranks first. This is unparalleled in the decline of national physique. Although the causes are very complex, the pathogen is the tubercle bacillus. After this bacterium invades the lungs, its nature is particularly stubborn, and treatment is often ineffective. Moreover, this disease is actually a contagious disease. 60% of children aged 10 to 15 are infected, and the number of infected adults is also considerable. It is truly terrifying. This must be prevented quickly. There are many methods: (1) Do not spit anywhere, do not cough at people, (2) Implement early treatment and X-ray examination, (3) All people suspected of having the disease should be regarded as contaminated with germs, so they should not be used by family members or outsiders, (4) People with the disease should be isolated for treatment, which can reduce the infection of more than three people, (5) Do not engage in excessive exercise, and other things such as not worrying and not overworking can all curb the spread of lung disease, which are also the keys to preventing lung disease. According to various countries in the world, the prevention of the rampant tuberculosis is unusually thorough. The United States spends 200 million gold yuan every year on tuberculosis prevention work, so the number of tuberculosis patients is decreasing day by day. Recently, celebrities from all walks of life have also organized a China Anti-Tuberculosis Association. Since its establishment, the number of members who have joined has been very enthusiastic. The purpose of the association is purely to prevent the occurrence of tuberculosis in the healthy public. If people from all walks of life wish to join, they only need to *** a small membership fee and will enjoy great benefits in the future.

Reading Q&A Reading Guidance:

A Preliminary Guide to Reading Social Sciences (I) 210

Reading Guidance:

My knowledge is shallow, but I am also someone whose desire for knowledge has not disappeared. Recently, the "Reading Consultant" in the Shen Bao has given me a glimmer of hope in the darkness.

I read it almost every day, but unfortunately, many of the topics discussed are either different from my living environment or do not match my level. Therefore, I am still not satisfied and cannot find any guidance. I think: the guide is to show the way for those who have doubts about reading, and there is no limit to the level or class that one must reach in order to receive guidance. Therefore, I venture to use this simple language to write about my reading problems and seek advice;

My living environment is of course very poor, but in addition to working for a living, I also have some spare time for myself, so reading has also become a problem for me. I am probably influenced by my friends who often talk about social thought, and by seeing many bad phenomena exposed in social reality. I have developed a great interest in social sciences, so I have read some social science books in the past two or three years. However, like me, who has no foundation in social sciences and cannot read Western languages, blindly reading those profound books is like a blind person riding a blind horse. I have spent a lot of valuable time, but the benefits are still limited.

Some of my friends are more knowledgeable than me. Sometimes I ask them for advice or ask them to recommend books to read, but because they are influenced by the theories of various sociological schools in the current society, their views are inconsistent, and the books they recommend are also different. This only makes me more confused.

Recently, a friend told me: "If you want to understand the truth and future of society, economics is of course the subject you should study, but you must also have a considerable understanding of law and politics! It is best for you to understand economics clearly now, (but they didn't point out which books), and then read some books on the outlines of law and politics, and then read history and geography. It is impossible to build a very tall building in one step."

But how can I not know that learning is not a short-term matter! Isn't it because I am poor and cannot enjoy the privilege of that kind of aristocratic education! The day before yesterday, I went to the library and saw that there were more than a thousand books in the economics category alone. Moreover, I have to steal time from my busy schedule to read them. Even if I spend all my time on it all day long, I don't know how much I will accomplish in a year! And the other subjects of politics, law, history, and geography are outside of that.

Guidance, Student: What do you think I should do! I don't want to become a sociologist, I just want to know where society will go in the future. In this case, how many and what kind of books should I read? Which category should I read first? I pray that you will give me good advice so that I, a lost person in the sea of books, can find a bright path.

Chun Qiu

Agile and Accurate 211

— Zhou Limin

Success is the precious child produced by a pair of parents: agility and accuracy.

No matter which successful person it is, in their life, there will always be important moments of "a single hair holding a thousand pounds" and "fleeting opportunities". At such times, if the mind wavers or hesitates, or if one is at a loss, all efforts will be wasted and nothing will be achieved!

A person who acts quickly when facing a problem will eventually succeed, even if they occasionally make mistakes; a person who delays and procrastinates will eventually fail, even if they have better judgment.

If a person unfortunately becomes a victim of "hesitation", their only savior is "agile decision-making and decisive action"!

In addition to being agile, one must also be accurate. The most common yet sacred accuracy in social interaction is keeping appointments. If one makes an appointment with someone for a certain time and then fails to show up or is late, unless there is a truly compelling reason, it is an intentional act of deception. In the new morality, this is a deeply rooted evil trait that must be avoided. Napoleon once invited several of his generals to dinner. When the appointed time arrived, the generals had not yet arrived, so he devoured a ton of food by himself. When they arrived, he had already finished eating. He stood up, left his seat, and said to them, "Gentlemen, the time for dinner has passed. We must go to work immediately"!

Agility is the mother of trust. Agility best demonstrates that we handle affairs in an orderly manner and do them well, making people trust our abilities. As for those who keep time accurately, they are often able to keep their promises, which means they are reliable people.

Color 212

— Zhang Yuming

Red, yellow, and blue are called "primary colors". All other colors that are formed by mixing primary colors are called "secondary colors". White can reflect light and is good at radiating heat, making it suitable for summer and spring. It is called a "cool color". Black and red have the opposite function of white and are named "warm colors". The Arctic region is extremely cold, with snow and ice everywhere, so the birds and animals produced there often have white feathers. The temperate zone has a mild climate, and in the spring and summer, the grass and trees are green, so the insects that are born at that time are mostly green. This is what is called a uniquely endowed protective color. The golden powders of the Southern Dynasties and the rouge of the Northern regions are the pink color that aesthetic poets use to praise beautiful women. Buddhists say: "Form is emptiness, and emptiness is form," which inspires people not to indulge in form. Blue shirts, blue eagle movements, red terror, and white imperialism are all colors used to classify political factions. A depressed society presents a decadent and withered appearance, deeply shrouded in a gloomy atmosphere. This symbolizes the grayness of society. Those who betray filial piety advocate the doctrine of opposing "filial piety is the first of all virtues". What is there to talk about "providing for one's parents"? Small gangsters engage in petty disputes, and the next thing you know, they are saying "I'll show you what's what!". In fact, isn't the open and secret fighting between people and people, countries and countries, also a kind of "I'll show you what's what!" behavior? What doctrines liberate people and give them freedom? What doctrines loudly proclaim national equality? But the facts show us that it is just like the lives of Moroccan women imprisoned in "black cages". This bizarre society really confuses people!

Eating and Watching 213

— Shen Shou Ruo

Female employees were given the nickname "vases" by male employees, so they retaliated with the name "rice buckets". In fact, these two things are very good together, called "have something to eat and have something to look at."

The only gift for the working class is a pancake and fried dough stick. On the surface, it is not as exquisite as the sweets enjoyed by the bourgeoisie; but in reality, it is exceptionally fragrant and crispy, and its taste is delicious. This is the same as the saying: "A country girl has something to eat but nothing to look at." Why do flatterers only have the impression of rich people in their minds and no image of poor people in their eyes? This is probably because the poor have "nothing to eat and nothing to look at"!

Evening in My Hometown 214

— Wei Zhong

Several days of snow have brought the cold of deep winter. It's the end of the year, just the time for farmers who have been working hard all year round to rest and recuperate.

In the twilight of evening, when the sun and moon alternate, night seizes the opportunity to expand its power and quickly spreads its net, covering the earth. I, a wanderer who has been away from home for many years, return to my long-departed hometown like a ghost, and wander alone on the streets I haven't been to for many years.

On the street, rows of wooden telephone poles stand in a straight line. The button-sized lamp heads emit starlight, flickering weakly and powerlessly in the dark sky.

At the end of the year, when the weather is cold, the fields no longer need a lot of labor from the farmers. They feel bored and restless at home. They sell the autumn grain, and there are still a few coins in their pockets. Although they still owe rent and have nothing to pawn, what can the price of two or three dollars per load of grain be used for? Therefore, they simply gather on the streets to eat, drink, gamble, and pursue temporary pleasure and intoxication. Especially at night, the streets of this small town in the countryside become unusually lively.

In the wine shop, seven or eight square tables are scattered around. White liquor, beef, and salted soybeans are served. Purple and swollen muscles, bloodshot eyes, throats like bamboo pipes, and liver-colored drunken faces create a chaotic and confusing scene with nonsense, dreams, and drunken words. Although there is no luxury of a wine hall, no pink curtains, no seductive maids, and no high-quality brandy or whiskey, madness, pleasure, and intoxication are pursued on the edge.

Under the thatched shed and in the broken house, bodies like firewood are curled up on a board that is a little over a foot high. Under the shadow of a bean-sized lamp, ginger-yellow and wax-like faces are faintly visible. Red pills, morphine, and opium are present. In the shadows, the giant hand of the god of death grabs the lives of everyone. Death, death, death. Scorched smoke is blown, sucked, and spat out, filling every corner and every alley.

"Long three, four five, yao er!" Entering, leaving, white tiger, green dragon, lying across, legs crossed, single bet, no hit, open! In the teahouse, three square tables are connected in a line, crowded with black heads and beating black hearts. Dice, bowls, dealers, and assistants beat, beat, beat. The skilled tone of calling bets, hope, doubt, and disappointment drill in and out of every gambler's heart. Status, life, and property are all staked on a single throw!

Therefore, the nights in this small town in the countryside are lively, warm, and thriving, like spring in winter. However, poverty, cold, and death have followed closely behind!

I, a wanderer who has been away from home for many years, return to my hometown like a ghost, and wander alone on the streets I haven't been to for many years.

Mistaken Identity 215

In the tram, passenger A reached into his pocket and found that his wallet was missing. He quickly grabbed passenger B.

Passenger A: "You stole my wallet." Just then, A reached into another pocket and found his wallet there. He blushed and apologized to B, saying, "I'm sorry, I'm sorry, I'm very sorry, please forgive me." Passenger B said coldly, "It doesn't matter. You mistook me for a pickpocket, but I mistook you for a gentleman."

Staying Up Late Warming Dreams, Singing Long Nights

Zi Qiang said: With such good intentions, let alone two liang of wine, even two jin of wine, I have to force myself to drink. Come, come, I'm bothering you. As he said, he held up his wine glass high, waiting for Gui Zhi to pour. Gui Zhi indeed stood by his side and filled his glass, then poured himself one as well. Then he sat down, raised his glass in salute, and slowly sipped. Gui Zhi had placed a large kerosene lamp with a shade, and Zi Qiang, sitting opposite, saw that her cheeks were red, and her upper eyelids were drooping. Even before drinking, it seemed as if she was already somewhat tipsy. He laughed: Are we really going to sit here until dawn tonight? Gui Zhi looked at him and smiled: That's what we agreed on, can I go back on my word? But you are a traveler tomorrow. If you are afraid you can't hold on, you can go back and rest. As he was speaking, a distant sound of "dang-dang qiang-qiang" reached his ears. It turned out that there were also two watchmen on this Hai Dian Main Street. That was the sound of the clapper and gong. Zi Qiang held his cup in his hand and tilted his ear to listen, saying: What time is it now? Gui Zhi raised his cup and said: Let's drink. Who cares what time it is? Zi Qiang said: You've already moved the clock in the house away, and I can't hear the gong either. When it's time to leave, I won't know. Gui Zhi opened the cabinet door, and the clock was placed inside, but the back of the clock face was facing out, while the front was facing in. He closed the cabinet and lifted a long coat on the clothes rack. A thick rope was tied to an alarm clock, hanging on the clothes hook. It was also facing out. Zi Qiang laughed: You still have the temperament of a child, so naughty. As he said, he stood up and reached out to take the alarm clock to look at. Gui Zhi reached out and blocked Zi Qiang. He laughed: When the time comes, the alarm clock will naturally tell you. What are you rushing for? Zi Qiang sat down and nodded, saying: I understand your meaning, all right, I won't look at the clock, I'll still sit down and drink. So he picked up his wine glass and drank half of it first. (317)
